# Investigation: DRA AllocationMode API Change Impact Analysis

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes
**Task Type:** Impact Analysis (investigation only — no code changes)

## Scenario

The Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) scheduler plugin is being modified to allow `AllocationMode: All` from multi-node resource pools. Previously, this allocation mode was restricted to single-node pools only. Before this change ships, the team needs a comprehensive impact analysis.

## Your Task

Produce an impact analysis report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. All source files that reference `AllocationMode` or the DRA allocation logic
2. Which controllers and schedulers are affected
3. What test files cover the current allocation behavior
4. What performance implications exist (scheduler hot paths affected)
5. Which downstream consumers (kubelet, device plugins) would see changed behavior
6. Risk assessment: what could break if this change has bugs

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Scope of the change — what components are affected and why>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted, categorized by risk level>

## Recommendation
<Risk mitigation strategy and testing plan>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on tracing `AllocationMode` through the DRA plugin, scheduler framework, and kubelet

    27→// claimStore manages all ResourceClaims for the pod, whether they were
    28→// created by the user directly (ResourceClaim) or indirectly (ResourceClaimTemplate)
    29→// as well as the special ResourceClaim for extended resources.
    30→//
    31→// The zero value is usable and empty.
    32→type claimStore struct {
    33→	// claims contains all user-owned claims, optionally followed by the special ResourceClaim for extended resources.
    34→	claims []*resourceapi.ResourceClaim
    35→	// numUserOwned is the number of claims without the special ResourceClaim.
    36→	numUserOwned int
    37→	// initialExtendedResourceClaimUID is the initial extended resource claim UID from PreFilter phase.
    38→	// It is different from the UID set by API server when the in-memory, temproary claim is written to the API server in PreBind phase.
    39→	initialExtendedResourceClaimUID types.UID
    40→}

    32→
    33→// foreachAllocatedDevice invokes the provided callback for each
    34→// device in the claim's allocation result which was allocated
    35→// exclusively for the claim.
    36→//
    37→// Devices allocated with admin access can be shared with other
    38→// claims and are skipped without invoking the callback.
    39→//

    18→
    19→import (
    20→	v1 "k8s.io/api/core/v1"
    21→	resourceapi "k8s.io/api/resource/v1"
    22→	fwk "k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework"
    23→)
    24→
    25→func DeviceClassMapping(draManager fwk.SharedDRAManager) (map[v1.ResourceName]string, error) {
    26→	classes, err := draManager.DeviceClasses().List()
    27→	extendedResources := make(map[v1.ResourceName]string, len(classes))
    28→	if err != nil {
    29→		return nil, err
    30→	}
    31→	for _, c := range classes {
    32→		if c.Spec.ExtendedResourceName != nil {
    33→			extendedResources[v1.ResourceName(*c.Spec.ExtendedResourceName)] = c.Name
    34→		}
    35→		extendedResources[v1.ResourceName(resourceapi.ResourceDeviceClassPrefix+c.Name)] = c.Name
    36→	}
    37→	return extendedResources, nil
    38→}

    36→// healthInfoCache is a cache of known device health.

    38→	sync.RWMutex
    39→	HealthInfo *state.DevicesHealthMap
    40→	stateFile  string
    41→}
    42→
    43→// newHealthInfoCache creates a new cache, loading from a checkpoint if present.
    44→func newHealthInfoCache(stateFile string) (*healthInfoCache, error) {
    45→	cache := &healthInfoCache{
    46→		HealthInfo: &state.DevicesHealthMap{},
    47→		stateFile:  stateFile,
    48→	}
    49→	if err := cache.loadFromCheckpoint(); err != nil {
    50→		klog.Background().Error(err, "Failed to load health checkpoint, proceeding with empty cache")
    51→	}
    52→	return cache, nil
    53→}

    30→
    31→func nodeMatches(node *v1.Node, nodeNameToMatch string, allNodesMatch bool, nodeSelector *v1.NodeSelector) (bool, error) {
    32→	switch {
    33→	case nodeNameToMatch != "":
    34→		return node != nil && node.Name == nodeNameToMatch, nil
    35→	case allNodesMatch:
    36→		return true, nil
    37→	case nodeSelector != nil:
    38→		selector, err := nodeaffinity.NewNodeSelector(nodeSelector)
    39→		if err != nil {
    40→			return false, fmt.Errorf("failed to parse node selector %s: %w", nodeSelector.String(), err)
    41→		}
    42→		return selector.Match(node), nil
    43→	}
    44→
    45→	return false, nil
    46→}

    49→	driver, pool string
    50→}

   150→
   151→func addSlice(pools map[PoolID]*Pool, s *resourceapi.ResourceSlice) error {
   152→	var slice draapi.ResourceSlice
   153→	if err := draapi.Convert_v1_ResourceSlice_To_api_ResourceSlice(s, &slice, nil); err != nil {
   154→		return fmt.Errorf("convert ResourceSlice: %w", err)
   155→	}
   156→
   157→	id := PoolID{Driver: slice.Spec.Driver, Pool: slice.Spec.Pool.Name}
   158→	pool := pools[id]
   159→	if pool == nil {
   160→		// New pool.
   161→		pool = &Pool{
   162→			PoolID: id,
   163→			Slices: []*draapi.ResourceSlice{&slice},
   164→		}
   165→		pools[id] = pool
   166→		return nil
   167→	}
   168→
   169→	if slice.Spec.Pool.Generation < pool.Slices[0].Spec.Pool.Generation {
   170→		// Out-dated.
   171→		return nil
   172→	}
   173→
   174→	if slice.Spec.Pool.Generation > pool.Slices[0].Spec.Pool.Generation {
   175→		// Newer, replaces all old slices.
   176→		pool.Slices = nil
   177→	}
   178→
   179→	// Add to pool.
   180→	pool.Slices = append(pool.Slices, &slice)
   181→	return nil
   182→}
   183→
   184→func poolIsInvalid(pool *Pool) (bool, string) {
   185→	devices := sets.New[draapi.UniqueString]()
   186→	for _, slice := range pool.Slices {
   187→		for _, device := range slice.Spec.Devices {
   188→			if devices.Has(device.Name) {
   189→				return true, fmt.Sprintf("duplicate device name %s", device.Name)
   190→			}
   191→			devices.Insert(device.Name)
   192→		}
   193→	}
   194→	return false, ""
   195→}
   196→

   198→	PoolID
   199→	IsIncomplete  bool
   200→	IsInvalid     bool
   201→	InvalidReason string

  1098→// isDRAExtendedResource checks if the specified resource for a given container
  1099→// in the provided pod is an extended resource managed by DRA.
  1100→func isDRAExtendedResource(pod *v1.Pod, containerName, resourceName string) bool {
  1101→	claimStatus := pod.Status.ExtendedResourceClaimStatus
  1102→	if claimStatus != nil {
  1103→		for _, resMap := range claimStatus.RequestMappings {
  1104→			if resMap.ContainerName == containerName && resMap.ResourceName == resourceName {
  1105→				return true
  1106→			}
  1107→		}
  1108→	}
  1109→	return false
  1110→}

   918→func (alloc *allocator) selectorsMatch(r requestIndices, device *draapi.Device, deviceID DeviceID, class *resourceapi.DeviceClass, selectors []resourceapi.DeviceSelector) (bool, error) {
   919→	for i, selector := range selectors {
   920→		expr := alloc.celCache.GetOrCompile(selector.CEL.Expression)
   921→		if expr.Error != nil {
   922→			// Could happen if some future apiserver accepted some
   923→			// future expression and then got downgraded. Normally
   924→			// the "stored expression" mechanism prevents that, but
   925→			// this code here might be more than one release older
   926→			// than the cluster it runs in.
   927→			if class != nil {
   928→				return false, fmt.Errorf("class %s: selector #%d: CEL compile error: %w", class.Name, i, expr.Error)
   929→			}
   930→			return false, fmt.Errorf("claim %s: selector #%d: CEL compile error: %w", klog.KObj(alloc.claimsToAllocate[r.claimIndex]), i, expr.Error)
   931→		}
   932→
   933→		// If this conversion turns out to be expensive, the CEL package could be converted
   934→		// to use unique strings.
   935→		var d resourceapi.Device
   936→		if err := draapi.Convert_api_Device_To_v1_Device(device, &d, nil); err != nil {
   937→			return false, fmt.Errorf("convert Device: %w", err)
   938→		}
   939→		matches, details, err := expr.DeviceMatches(alloc.ctx, cel.Device{Driver: deviceID.Driver.String(), Attributes: d.Attributes, Capacity: d.Capacity})
   940→		if class != nil {
   941→			alloc.logger.V(7).Info("CEL result", "device", deviceID, "class", klog.KObj(class), "selector", i, "expression", selector.CEL.Expression, "matches", matches, "actualCost", ptr.Deref(details.ActualCost(), 0), "err", err)
   942→		} else {
   943→			alloc.logger.V(7).Info("CEL result", "device", deviceID, "claim", klog

    36→// healthInfoCache is a cache of known device health.
    37→type healthInfoCache struct {
    38→	sync.RWMutex
    39→	HealthInfo *state.DevicesHealthMap
    40→	stateFile  string
    41→}
    42→
    43→// newHealthInfoCache creates a new cache, loading from a checkpoint if present.
    44→func newHealthInfoCache(stateFile string) (*healthInfoCache, error) {
    45→	cache := &healthInfoCache{
    46→		HealthInfo: &state.DevicesHealthMap{},
    47→		stateFile:  stateFile,
    48→	}
    49→	if err := cache.loadFromCheckpoint(); err != nil {
    50→		klog.Background().Error(err, "Failed to load health checkpoint, proceeding with empty cache")
    51→	}
    52→	return cache, nil
    53→}

type constraint interface {
	// add is called whenever a device is about to be allocated. It must
	// check whether the device matches the constraint and if yes,
	// track that it is allocated.
	add(requestName, subRequestName string, device *draapi.Device, deviceID DeviceID) bool

	// For every successful add there is exactly one matching removed call
	// with the exact same parameters.
	remove(requestName, subRequestName string, device *draapi.Device, deviceID DeviceID)
}

// matchAttributeConstraint compares an attribute value across devices.
// All devices must share the same value. When the set of devices is
// empty, any device that has the attribute can be added. After that,
// only matching devices can be added.
//

    31→func nodeMatches(node *v1.Node, nodeNameToMatch string, allNodesMatch bool, nodeSelector *v1.NodeSelector) (bool, error) {
    32→	switch {
    33→	case nodeNameToMatch != "":
    34→		return node != nil && node.Name == nodeNameToMatch, nil
    35→	case allNodesMatch:
    36→		return true, nil
    37→	case nodeSelector != nil:
    38→		selector, err := nodeaffinity.NewNodeSelector(nodeSelector)
    39→		if err != nil {
    40→			return false, fmt.Errorf("failed to parse node selector %s: %w", nodeSelector.String(), err)
    41→		}
    42→		return selector.Match(node), nil
    43→	}
    44→
    45→	return false, nil
    46→}

366-assistanttext-
The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here's a brief summary of the findings:

**What the change does:** Commit `2e534d6da10` fixes `GatherPools()` in all three allocator tiers to compute pool completeness _before_ filtering slices by node affinity. Previously, multi-node pools were always marked `IsIncomplete` (false positive) because the post-filter slice count didn't match `ResourceSliceCount`, which blocked `AllocationMode: All` from working with multi-node pools.

**Key findings:**
- **4 files changed** across stable/incubating/experimental pool code + test infrastructure
- **556 total AllocationMode references** across 56 files in the codebase
- **Scheduler hot path impact:** `GatherPools()` runs inside the `Filter` extension point for every candidate node — the change adds a double-pass over all slices
- **Kubelet is unaffected code-wise** but will process different allocation results (more devices per claim from multi-node pools)
- **A revert commit exists** (`a0e500ace39`), indicating this change was previously landed and reverted — warranting extra scrutiny
- **Primary risk:** False-negative `IsIncomplete` could cause partial device allocation; kubelet DRA driver failures if allocation references devices not present on the node

If the entire\n   317\u2192\t// status is as before, then something else must have changed\n   318\u2192\t// and we don't care. What happens in practice is that the\n   319\u2192\t// resource driver adds the finalizer.\n   320\u2192\tif apiequality.Semantic.DeepEqual(&originalClaim.Status, &modifiedClaim.Status) {\n   321\u2192\t\tif loggerV := logger.V(7); loggerV.Enabled() {\n   322\u2192\t\t\t// Log more information.\n   323\u2192\t\t\tloggerV.Info(\"claim for pod got modified where the pod doesn't care\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"claim\", klog.KObj(modifiedClaim), \"diff\", diff.Diff(originalClaim, modifiedClaim))\n   324\u2192\t\t} else {\n   325\u2192\t\t\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"claim for pod got modified where the pod doesn't care\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"claim\", klog.KObj(modifiedClaim))\n   326\u2192\t\t}\n   327\u2192\t\treturn fwk.QueueSkip, nil\n   328\u2192\t}\n   329\u2192\n   330\u2192\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"status of claim for pod got updated\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"claim\", klog.KObj(modifiedClaim))\n   331\u2192\treturn fwk.Queue, nil\n   332\u2192}\n   333\u2192\n   334\u2192// isSchedulableAfterPodChange is invoked for update pod events reported by\n   335\u2192// an informer. It checks whether that change adds the ResourceClaim(s) that the\n   336\u2192// pod has been waiting for.\n   337\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterPodChange(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (fwk.QueueingHint, error) {\n   338\u2192\t_, modifiedPod, err := schedutil.As[*v1.Pod](nil, newObj)\n   339\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   340\u2192\t\t// Shouldn't happen.\n   341\u2192\t\treturn fwk.Queue, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected object in isSchedulableAfterClaimChange: %w\", err)\n   342\u2192\t}\n   343\u2192\n   344\u2192\tif pod.UID != modifiedPod.UID {\n   345\u2192\t\tlogger.V(7).Info(\"pod is not schedulable after change in other pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"modifiedPod\", klog.KObj(modifiedPod))\n   346\u2192\t\treturn fwk.QueueSkip, nil\n   347\u2192\t}\n   348\u2192\n   349\u2192\tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(modifiedPod, nil); err != nil {\n   350\u2192\t\t// This is not an unexpected error: we know that\n   351\u2192\t\t// foreachPodResourceClaim only returns errors for \"not\n   352\u2192\t\t// schedulable\".\n   353\u2192\t\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"pod is not schedulable after being updated\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n   354\u2192\t\treturn fwk.QueueSkip, nil\n   355\u2192\t}\n   356\u2192\n   357\u2192\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"pod got updated and is schedulable\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod))\n   358\u2192\treturn fwk.Queue, nil\n   359\u2192}\n   360\u2192\n   361\u2192// podResourceClaims returns the ResourceClaims for all pod.Spec.PodResourceClaims.\n   362\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) podResourceClaims(pod *v1.Pod) ([]*resourceapi.ResourceClaim, error) {\n   363\u2192\tclaims := make([]*resourceapi.ResourceClaim, 0, len(pod.Spec.ResourceClaims))\n   364\u2192\tif err := pl.foreachPodResourceClaim(pod, func(_ string, claim *resourceapi.ResourceClaim) {\n   365\u2192\t\t// We store the pointer as returned by the lister. The\n   366\u2192\t\t// assumption is that if a claim gets modified while our code\n   367\u2192\t\t// runs, the cache will store a new pointer, not mutate the\n   368\u2192\t\t// existing object that we point to here.\n   369\u2192\t\tclaims = append(claims, claim)\n   370\u2192\t}); err != nil {\n   371\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   372\u2192\t}\n   373\u2192\treturn claims, nil\n   374\u2192}\n   375\u2192\n   376\u2192// foreachPodResourceClaim checks that each ResourceClaim for the pod exists.\n   377\u2192// It calls an optional handler for those claims that it finds.\n   378\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) foreachPodResourceClaim(pod *v1.Pod, cb func(podResourceName string, claim *resourceapi.ResourceClaim)) error {\n   379\u2192\tfor _, resource := range pod.Spec.ResourceClaims {\n   380\u2192\t\tclaimName, mustCheckOwner, err := resourceclaim.Name(pod, &resource)\n   381\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   382\u2192\t\t\treturn err\n   383\u2192\t\t}\n   384\u2192\t\t// The claim name might be nil if no underlying resource claim\n   385\u2192\t\t// was generated for the referenced claim. There are valid use\n   386\u2192\t\t// cases when this might happen, so we simply skip it.\n   387\u2192\t\tif claimName == nil {\n   388\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   389\u2192\t\t}\n   390\u2192\t\tclaim, err := pl.draManager.ResourceClaims().Get(pod.Namespace, *claimName)\n   391\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   392\u2192\t\t\treturn err\n   393\u2192\t\t}\n   394\u2192\n   395\u2192\t\tif claim.DeletionTimestamp != nil {\n   396\u2192\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"resourceclaim %q is being deleted\", claim.Name)\n   397\u2192\t\t}\n   398\u2192\n   399\u2192\t\tif mustCheckOwner {\n   400\u2192\t\t\tif err := resourceclaim.IsForPod(pod, claim); err != nil {\n   401\u2192\t\t\t\treturn err\n   402\u2192\t\t\t}\n   403\u2192\t\t}\n   404\u2192\t\tif cb != nil {\n   405\u2192\t\t\tcb(resource.Name, claim)\n   406\u2192\t\t}\n   407\u2192\t}\n   408\u2192\treturn nil\n   409\u2192}\n   410\u2192\n   411\u2192// hasDeviceClassMappedExtendedResource returns true when the given resource list has an extended resource, that has\n   412\u2192// a mapping to a device class.\n   413\u2192func hasDeviceClassMappedExtendedResource(reqs v1.ResourceList, deviceClassMapping map[v1.ResourceName]string) bool {\n   414\u2192\tfor rName, rValue := range reqs {\n   415\u2192\t\tif rValue.IsZero() {\n   416\u2192\t\t\t// We only care about the resources requested by the pod we are trying to schedule.\n   417\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   418\u2192\t\t}\n   419\u2192\t\tif schedutil.IsDRAExtendedResourceName(rName) {\n   420\u2192\t\t\t_, ok := deviceClassMapping[rName]\n   421\u2192\t\t\tif ok {\n   422\u2192\t\t\t\treturn true\n   423\u2192\t\t\t}\n   424\u2192\t\t}\n   425\u2192\t}\n   426\u2192\treturn false\n   427\u2192}\n   428\u2192\n   429\u2192// findExtendedResourceClaim looks for the extended resource claim, i.e., the claim with special annotation\n   430\u2192// set to \"true\", and with the pod as owner. It must be called with all ResourceClaims in the cluster.\n   431\u2192// The returned ResourceClaim is read-only.\n   432\u2192func findExtendedResourceClaim(pod *v1.Pod, resourceClaims []*resourceapi.ResourceClaim) *resourceapi.ResourceClaim {\n   433\u2192\tfor _, c := range resourceClaims {\n   434\u2192\t\tif c.Annotations[resourceapi.ExtendedResourceClaimAnnotation] == \"true\" {\n   435\u2192\t\t\tfor _, or := range c.OwnerReferences {\n   436\u2192\t\t\t\tif or.Name == pod.Name && *or.Controller && or.UID == pod.UID {\n   437\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn c\n   438\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   439\u2192\t\t\t}\n   440\u2192\t\t}\n   441\u2192\t}\n   442\u2192\treturn nil\n   443\u2192}\n   444\u2192\n   445\u2192// preFilterExtendedResources checks if there is any extended resource in the\n   446\u2192// pod requests that has a device class mapping, i.e., there is a device class\n   447\u2192// that has spec.ExtendedResourceName or its implicit extended resource name\n   448\u2192// matching the given extended resource in that pod requests.\n   449\u2192//\n   450\u2192// It looks for the special resource claim for the pod created from prior scheduling\n   451\u2192// cycle. If not found, it creates the special claim with no Requests in the Spec,\n   452\u2192// with a temporary UID, and the specialClaimInMemName name.\n   453\u2192// Either way, the special claim is stored in state.claims.\n   454\u2192//\n   455\u2192// In addition, draExtendedResource is also stored in the cycle state.\n   456\u2192//\n   457\u2192// It returns the special ResourceClaim and an error status. It returns nil for both\n   458\u2192// if the feature is disabled or not required for the Pod.\n   459\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) preFilterExtendedResources(pod *v1.Pod, logger klog.Logger, s *stateData) (*resourceapi.ResourceClaim, *fwk.Status) {\n   460\u2192\tif !pl.fts.EnableDRAExtendedResource {\n   461\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil\n   462\u2192\t}\n   463\u2192\n   464\u2192\tdeviceClassMapping, err := extended.DeviceClassMapping(pl.draManager)\n   465\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   466\u2192\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, err, \"retrieving extended resource to DeviceClass mapping\")\n   467\u2192\t}\n   468\u2192\n   469\u2192\treqs := resourcehelper.PodRequests(pod, resourcehelper.PodResourcesOptions{})\n   470\u2192\thasExtendedResource := hasDeviceClassMappedExtendedResource(reqs, deviceClassMapping)\n   471\u2192\tif !hasExtendedResource {\n   472\u2192\t\treturn nil, nil\n   473\u2192\t}\n   474\u2192\n   475\u2192\ts.draExtendedResource.resourceToDeviceClass = deviceClassMapping\n   476\u2192\tr := framework.NewResource(reqs)\n   477\u2192\ts.draExtendedResource.podScalarResources = r.ScalarResources\n   478\u2192\n   479\u2192\tresourceClaims, err := pl.draManager.ResourceClaims().List()\n   480\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   481\u2192\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, err, \"listing ResourceClaims\")\n   482\u2192\t}\n   483\u2192\n   484\u2192\t// Check if the special resource claim has been created from prior scheduling cycle.\n   485\u2192\t//\n   486\u2192\t// If it was already allocated earlier, that allocation might not be valid anymore.\n   487\u2192\t// We could try to check that, but it depends on various factors that are difficult to\n   488\u2192\t// cover (basically needs to replicate allocator logic) and if it turns out that the\n   489\u2192\t// allocation is stale, we would have to schedule with those allocated devices not\n   490\u2192\t// available for a new allocation. This situation should be rare (= binding failure),\n   491\u2192\t// so we solve it via brute-force\n   492\u2192\t// - Kick off deallocation in the background.\n   493\u2192\t// - Mark the pod as unschedulable. Successful deallocation will make it schedulable again.\n   494\u2192\textendedResourceClaim := findExtendedResourceClaim(pod, resourceClaims)\n   495\u2192\tif extendedResourceClaim == nil {\n   496\u2192\t\t// Create one special claim for all extended resources backed by DRA in the Pod.\n   497\u2192\t\t// Create the ResourceClaim with pod as owner, with a generated name that uses\n   498\u2192\t\t// <pod name>-extended-resources- as base. The final name will get truncated if it\n   499\u2192\t\t// would be too long.\n   500\u2192\t\textendedResourceClaim = &resourceapi.ResourceClaim{\n   501\u2192\t\t\tObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{\n   502\u2192\t\t\t\tNamespace: pod.Namespace,\n   503\u2192\t\t\t\tName:      specialClaimInMemName,\n   504\u2192\t\t\t\t// fake temporary UID for use in SignalClaimPendingAllocation\n   505\u2192\t\t\t\tUID:          types.UID(uuid.NewUUID()),\n   506\u2192\t\t\t\tGenerateName: pod.Name + \"-extended-resources-\",\n   507\u2192\t\t\t\tOwnerReferences: []metav1.OwnerReference{\n   508\u2192\t\t\t\t\t{\n   509\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tAPIVersion: \"v1\",\n   510\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tKind:       \"Pod\",\n   511\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tName:       pod.Name,\n   512\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tUID:        pod.UID,\n   513\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tController: ptr.To(true),\n   514\u2192\t\t\t\t\t},\n   515\u2192\t\t\t\t},\n   516\u2192\t\t\t\tAnnotations: map[string]string{\n   517\u2192\t\t\t\t\tresourceapi.ExtendedResourceClaimAnnotation: \"true\",\n   518\u2192\t\t\t\t},\n   519\u2192\t\t\t},\n   520\u2192\t\t\tSpec: resourceapi.ResourceClaimSpec{},\n   521\u2192\t\t}\n   522\u2192\t}\n   523\u2192\treturn extendedResourceClaim, nil\n   524\u2192}\n   525\u2192\n   526\u2192// PreFilter invoked at the prefilter extension point to check if pod has all\n   527\u2192// immediate claims bound. UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is returned if\n   528\u2192// the pod cannot be scheduled at the moment on any node.\n   529\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) PreFilter(ctx context.Context, state fwk.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []fwk.NodeInfo) (*fwk.PreFilterResult, *fwk.Status) {\n   530\u2192\tif !pl.enabled {\n   531\u2192\t\treturn nil, fwk.NewStatus(fwk.Skip)\n   532\u2192\t}\n   533\u2192\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   534\u2192\n   535\u2192\t// If the pod does not reference any claim, we don't need to do\n   536\u2192\t// anything for it. We just initialize an empty state to record that\n   537\u2192\t// observation for the other functions. This gets updated below\n   538\u2192\t// if we get that far.\n   539\u2192\ts := &stateData{}\n   540\u2192\tstate.Write(stateKey, s)\n   541\u2192\n   542\u2192\tuserClaims, err := pl.podResourceClaims(pod)\n   543\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   544\u2192\t\treturn nil, statusUnschedulable(logger, err.Error())\n   545\u2192\t}\n   546\u2192\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"pod resource claims\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"resourceclaims\", klog.KObjSlice(userClaims))\n   547\u2192\textendedResourceClaim, status := pl.preFilterExtendedResources(pod, logger, s)\n   548\u2192\tif status != nil {\n   549\u2192\t\treturn nil, status\n   550\u2192\t}\n   551\u2192\tclaims := newClaimStore(userClaims, extendedResourceClaim)\n   552\u2192\n   553\u2192\t// This check covers user and extended ResourceClaim.\n   554\u2192\tif claims.empty() {\n   555\u2192\t\treturn nil, fwk.NewStatus(fwk.Skip)\n   556\u2192\t}\n   557\u2192\n   558\u2192\t// Counts all claims which the scheduler needs to allocate itself.\n   559\u2192\tnumClaimsToAllocate := 0\n   560\u2192\ts.informationsForClaim = make([]informationForClaim, claims.len())\n   561\u2192\tfor index, claim := range claims.all() {\n   562\u2192\t\tif claim.Status.Allocation != nil &&\n   563\u2192\t\t\t!resourceclaim.CanBeReserved(claim) &&\n   564\u2192\t\t\t!resourceclaim.IsReservedForPod(pod, claim) {\n   565\u2192\t\t\t// Resource is in use. The pod has to wait.\n   566\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, statusUnschedulable(logger, \"resourceclaim in use\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"resourceclaim\", klog.KObj(claim))\n   567\u2192\t\t}\n   568\u2192\n   569\u2192\t\tif claim.Status.Allocation != nil {\n   570\u2192\t\t\tif claim.Status.Allocation.NodeSelector != nil {\n   571\u2192\t\t\t\tnodeSelector, err := nodeaffinity.NewNodeSelector(claim.Status.Allocation.NodeSelector)\n   572\u2192\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   573\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, err)\n   574\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   575\u2192\t\t\t\ts.informationsForClaim[index].availableOnNodes = nodeSelector\n   576\u2192\t\t\t}\n   577\u2192\t\t} else {\n   578\u2192\t\t\tnumClaimsToAllocate++\n   579\u2192\n   580\u2192\t\t\t// Allocation in flight? Better wait for that\n   581\u2192\t\t\t// to finish, see inFlightAllocations\n   582\u2192\t\t\t// documentation for details.\n   583\u2192\t\t\tif pl.draManager.ResourceClaims().ClaimHasPendingAllocation(claim.UID) {\n   584\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil, statusUnschedulable(logger, fmt.Sprintf(\"resource claim %s is in the process of being allocated\", klog.KObj(claim)))\n   585\u2192\t\t\t}\n   586\u2192\n   587\u2192\t\t\t// Continue without validating the special claim for extended resource backed by DRA.\n   588\u2192\t\t\t// For the claim template, it is not allocated yet at this point, and it does not have a spec.\n   589\u2192\t\t\t// For the claim from prior scheduling cycle, leave it to Filter Phase to validate.\n   590\u2192\t\t\tif claim == extendedResourceClaim {\n   591\u2192\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   592\u2192\t\t\t}\n   593\u2192\n   594\u2192\t\t\t// Check all requests and device classes. If a class\n   595\u2192\t\t\t// does not exist, scheduling cannot proceed, no matter\n   596\u2192\t\t\t// how the claim is being allocated.\n   597\u2192\t\t\t//\n   598\u2192\t\t\t// When using a control plane controller, a class might\n   599\u2192\t\t\t// have a node filter. This is useful for trimming the\n   600\u2192\t\t\t// initial set of potential nodes before we ask the\n   601\u2192\t\t\t// driver(s) for information about the specific pod.\n   602\u2192\t\t\tfor _, request := range claim.Spec.Devices.Requests {\n   603\u2192\t\t\t\t// The requirements differ depending on whether the request has a list of\n   604\u2192\t\t\t\t// alternative subrequests defined in the firstAvailable field.\n   605\u2192\t\t\t\tswitch {\n   606\u2192\t\t\t\tcase request.Exactly != nil:\n   607\u2192\t\t\t\t\tif status := pl.validateDeviceClass(logger, request.Exactly.DeviceClassName, request.Name); status != nil {\n   608\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, status\n   609\u2192\t\t\t\t\t}\n   610\u2192\t\t\t\tcase len(request.FirstAvailable) > 0:\n   611\u2192\t\t\t\t\tif !pl.fts.EnableDRAPrioritizedList {\n   612\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, statusUnschedulable(logger, fmt.Sprintf(\"resource claim %s, request %s: has subrequests, but the DRAPrioritizedList feature is disabled\", klog.KObj(claim), request.Name))\n   613\u2192\t\t\t\t\t}\n   614\u2192\t\t\t\t\tfor _, subRequest := range request.FirstAvailable {\n   615\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tqualRequestName := strings.Join([]string{request.Name, subRequest.Name}, \"/\")\n   616\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tif status := pl.validateDeviceClass(logger, subRequest.DeviceClassName, qualRequestName); status != nil {\n   617\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, status\n   618\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n   619\u2192\t\t\t\t\t}\n   620\u2192\t\t\t\tdefault:\n   621\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, statusUnschedulable(logger, fmt.Sprintf(\"resource claim %s, request %s: unknown request type\", klog.KObj(claim), request.Name))\n   622\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   623\u2192\t\t\t}\n   624\u2192\t\t}\n   625\u2192\t}\n   626\u2192\n   627\u2192\tif numClaimsToAllocate > 0 {\n   628\u2192\t\tif loggerV := logger.V(5); loggerV.Enabled() {\n   629\u2192\t\t\tclaimsToAllocate := make([]*resourceapi.ResourceClaim, 0, claims.len())\n   630\u2192\t\t\tfor _, claim := range claims.toAllocate() {\n   631\u2192\t\t\t\tclaimsToAllocate = append(claimsToAllocate, claim)\n   632\u2192\t\t\t}\n   633\u2192\t\t\tloggerV.Info(\"Preparing allocation with structured parameters\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"resourceclaims\", klog.KObjSlice(claimsToAllocate))\n   634\u2192\t\t}\n   635\u2192\n   636\u2192\t\t// Doing this over and over again for each pod could be avoided\n   637\u2192\t\t// by setting the allocator up once and then keeping it up-to-date\n   638\u2192\t\t// as changes are observed.\n   639\u2192\t\t//\n   640\u2192\t\t// But that would cause problems for using the plugin in the\n   641\u2192\t\t// Cluster Autoscaler. If this step here turns out to be\n   642\u2192\t\t// expensive, we may have to maintain and update state more\n   643\u2192\t\t// persistently.\n   644\u2192\t\t//\n   645\u2192\t\t// Claims (and thus their devices) are treated as \"allocated\" if they are in the assume cache\n   646\u2192\t\t// or currently their allocation is in-flight. This does not change\n   647\u2192\t\t// during filtering, so we can determine that once.\n   648\u2192\t\tvar allocatedState *structured.AllocatedState\n   649\u2192\t\tif pl.fts.EnableDRAConsumableCapacity {\n   650\u2192\t\t\tallocatedState, err = pl.draManager.ResourceClaims().GatherAllocatedState()\n   651\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   652\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, err)\n   653\u2192\t\t\t}\n   654\u2192\t\t\tif allocatedState == nil {\n   655\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, errors.New(\"nil allocated state\"))\n   656\u2192\t\t\t}\n   657\u2192\t\t} else {\n   658\u2192\t\t\tallocatedDevices, err := pl.draManager.ResourceClaims().ListAllAllocatedDevices()\n   659\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   660\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, err)\n   661\u2192\t\t\t}\n   662\u2192\t\t\tallocatedState = &structured.AllocatedState{\n   663\u2192\t\t\t\tAllocatedDevices:         allocatedDevices,\n   664\u2192\t\t\t\tAllocatedSharedDeviceIDs: sets.New[structured.SharedDeviceID](),\n   665\u2192\t\t\t\tAggregatedCapacity:       structured.NewConsumedCapacityCollection(),\n   666\u2192\t\t\t}\n   667\u2192\t\t}\n   668\u2192\t\tslices, err := pl.draManager.ResourceSlices().ListWithDeviceTaintRules()\n   669\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   670\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, err)\n   671\u2192\t\t}\n   672\u2192\t\tfeatures := allocatorFeatures(pl.fts)\n   673\u2192\t\tallocator, err := structured.NewAllocator(ctx, features, *allocatedState, pl.draManager.DeviceClasses(), slices, pl.celCache)\n   674\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   675\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, statusError(logger, err)\n   676\u2192\t\t}\n   677\u2192\t\ts.allocator = allocator\n   678\u2192\t\ts.nodeAllocations = make(map[string]nodeAllocation)\n   679\u2192\t}\n   680\u2192\ts.claims = claims\n   681\u2192\treturn nil, nil\n   682\u2192}\n   683\u2192\n   684\u2192func allocatorFeatures(fts feature.Features) structured.Features {\n   685\u2192\treturn structured.Features{\n   686\u2192\t\tAdminAccess:            fts.EnableDRAAdminAccess,\n   687\u2192\t\tPrioritizedList:        fts.EnableDRAPrioritizedList,\n   688\u2192\t\tPartitionableDevices:   fts.EnableDRAPartitionableDevices,\n   689\u2192\t\tDeviceTaints:           fts.EnableDRADeviceTaints,\n   690\u2192\t\tDeviceBindingAndStatus: fts.EnableDRADeviceBindingConditions && fts.EnableDRAResourceClaimDeviceStatus,\n   691\u2192\t\tConsumableCapacity:     fts.EnableDRAConsumableCapacity,\n   692\u2192\t}\n   693\u2192}\n   694\u2192\n   695\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) validateDeviceClass(logger klog.Logger, deviceClassName, requestName string) 709\u2192\treturn nil\n   710\u2192}\n   711\u2192\n   712\u2192// PreFilterExtensions returns prefilter extensions, pod add and remove.\n   713\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) PreFilterExtensions() fwk.PreFilterExtensions {\n   714\u2192\treturn nil\n   715\u2192}\n   716\u2192\n   717\u2192func getStateData(cs fwk.CycleState) (*stateData, error) {\n   718\u2192\tstate, err := *fwk.Status) {\n   737\u2192\textendedResourceClaim := state.claims.extendedResourceClaim()\n   738\u2192\tif extendedResourceClaim == nil {\n   739\u2192\t\t// Nothing to do.\n   740\u2192\t\treturn 776\u2192\t}\n   777\u2192\n   778\u2192\t// No extended resources backed by DRA on this node.\n   779\u2192\t// The pod may have extended resources, but they are all backed by device\n   780\u2192\t// plugin, hence the noderesources plugin should have checked if the node\n   781\u2192\t// can fit the pod.\n   782\u2192\t// This dynamic resources plugin Filter phase has nothing left to 813\u2192\t// iterating over the containers, and the resources in the containers,\n   814\u2192\t// and create one request per <container, extended resource>.\n   815\u2192\n   816\u2192\t// pod level 857\u2192\t\t\t// crq is the quantity of the extended resource request.\n   858\u2192\t\t\tdeviceRequests = append(deviceRequests,\n   859\u2192\t\t\t\tresourceapi.DeviceRequest{\n 869\u2192\tsort.Slice(deviceRequests, func(i, j int) bool {\n   870\u2192\t\treturn deviceRequests[i].Name < deviceRequests[j].Name\n   871\u2192\t})\n   872\u2192\treturn deviceRequests\n   873\u2192}\n   874\u2192\n   875\u2192// Filter invoked at the filter extension point.\n   876\u2192// It evaluates if a pod can fit due to the resources it requests,\n   877\u2192// for both allocated and unallocated claims.\n   878\u2192//\n   879\u2192// For claims that are bound, then it checks that the node affinity is\n   880\u2192// satisfied by the given node.\n   881\u2192//\n   882\u2192// For claims that are unbound, it checks whether the claim might get allocated\n   883\u2192// for the node.\n   884\u2192func (pl *DynamicResources) Filter(ctx context.Context, cs fwk.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo fwk.NodeInfo) *fwk.Status {\n   885\u2192\tif !pl.enabled {\n   886\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   887\u2192\t}\n   888\u2192\tstate, err := getStateData(cs)\n 921\u2192\t\t\t// anything else.\n   922\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   923\u2192\t\t}\n   924\u2192\n   925\u2192\t\t// The claim is allocated, check whether it is ready for binding.\n   926\u2192\t\tif 933\u2192\t\t\t}\n   934\u2192\t\t}\n   935\u2192\t}\n   936\u2192\n   937\u2192\t// Use allocator to check the node and cache the result in case that the node is picked.\n   938\u2192\tvar \"node\", klog.KObj(node), \"resourceclaims\", klog.KObjSlice(claimsToAllocate))\n   970\u2192\t\tcase err != nil:\n   971\u2192\t\t\t// This should only fail if there is something wrong with the claim or class.\n   972\u2192\t\t\t// Return an error to abort scheduling of it.\n   973\u2192\t\t\t//\n   974\u2192\t\t\t// This will cause retries. It would be slightly nicer to mark it as unschedulable\n   975\u2192\t\t\t// *and* abort scheduling. Then only cluster event for updating the claim or class\n   976\u2192\t\t\t// with the broken CEL expression would trigger rescheduling.\n   977\u2192\t\t\t//\n   978\u2192\t\t\t// But we cannot do both. As this shouldn't occur often, aborting like this is\n   979\u2192\t\t\t// better than the more complicated alternative (return Unschedulable here, remember\n   980\u2192\t\t\t// the error, then later raise it again later if needed).\n   981\u2192\t\t\treturn statusError(logger, err, \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", klog.KObj(node), \"resourceclaims\", klog.KObjSlice(claimsToAllocate))\n   982\u2192\t\t}\n   983\u2192\t\t// Check for exact length just to be sure. In practice this is all-or-nothing.\n   984\u2192\t\tif len(a) != len(claimsToAllocate) {\n   985\u2192\t\t\treturn statusUnschedulable(logger, \"cannot allocate all claims\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", klog.KObj(node), \"resourceclaims\", klog.KObjSlice(claimsToAllocate))\n   986\u2192\t\t}\n   987\u2192\t\t// Reserve uses this information.\n   988\u2192\t\tallocations = a\n   989\u2192\t}\n   990\u2192\n   991\u2192\t// Store information in state while holding the mutex.\n   992\u2192\tif state.allocator != nil || len(unavailableClaims) > 0 {\n   993\u2192\t\tstate.mutex.Lock()\n   994\u2192\t\tdefer state.mutex.Unlock()\n   995\u2192\t}\n   996\u2192\n   997\u2192\tif len(unavailableClaims) > 0 {\n   998\u2192\t\t// Remember all unavailable claims. If yes, it picks one and\n  1028\u2192// requests its deallocation. 1371\u2192// the second %d is the extended resource's index in that container's sorted resource requests.\n  1372\u2192func createRequestMappings(claim *resourceapi.ResourceClaim, pod *v1.Pod) 110\u2192\t// cache enables temporarily storing a newer claim object\n   111\u2192\t// while the scheduler has allocated it and the corresponding object\n   112\u2192\t// update from the apiserver has not been processed by the claim\n   113\u2192\t// informer callbacks. ResourceClaimTracker get added here in PreBind and removed by\n   114\u2192\t// the informer callback (based on the \"newer than\" comparison in the\n   115\u2192\t// assume cache).\n   116\u2192\t//\n   117\u2192\t// It uses cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc to generate object names, which\n   118\u2192\t// therefore are \"<namespace>/<name>\".\n   119\u2192\t//\n   120\u2192\t// This is necessary to ensure that reconstructing the resource usage\n   121\u2192\t// at the start of a pod scheduling cycle doesn't reuse the resources\n   122\u2192\t// assigned to such a claim. Alternatively, claim allocation state\n   123\u2192\t// could also get tracked across pod scheduling cycles, but that\n   124\u2192\t// - adds complexity (need to carefully sync state with informer events\n   125\u2192\t//   for claims and ResourceSlices)\n   126\u2192\t// - would make integration with cluster autoscaler harder because it would need\n   127\u2192\t//   to trigger informer callbacks.\n   128\u2192\tcache *assumecache.AssumeCache\n   129\u2192\t// inFlightAllocations is a map from claim UUIDs to claim objects for those claims\n   130\u2192\t// for which allocation was triggered during a scheduling cycle and the\n   131\u2192\t// corresponding claim status update call in PreBind has not been done\n   132\u2192\t// yet. If another pod needs the claim, the pod is treated as \"not\n   133\u2192\t// schedulable yet\". The cluster event for the claim status update will\n   134\u2192\t// make it schedulable.\n   135\u2192\t//\n   136\u2192\t// This mechanism avoids the following problem:\n   137\u2192\t// - Pod A triggers allocation for claim X.\n   138\u2192\t// - Pod B shares access to that claim and gets scheduled because\n   139\u2192\t//   the claim is assumed to be allocated.\n   140\u2192\t// - PreBind for pod B is called first, tries to update reservedFor and\n   141\u2192\t//   fails because the claim is not really allocated yet.\n   142\u2192\t//\n   143\u2192\t// We could avoid the ordering problem by allowing either pod A or pod B\n   144\u2192\t// to set the allocation. But that is more complicated and leads to another\n   145\u2192\t// problem:\n   146\u2192\t// - Pod A and B get scheduled as above.\n   147\u2192\t// - PreBind for pod A gets called first, then fails with a temporary API error.\n   148\u2192\t//   It removes the updated claim from the assume cache because of that.\n   149\u2192\t// - PreBind for pod B gets called next and succeeds with adding the\n   150\u2192\t//   allocation and its own reservedFor entry.\n   151\u2192\t// - The assume cache is now not reflecting that the claim is allocated,\n   152\u2192\t//   which could lead to reusing the same resource for some other claim.\n   153\u2192\t//\n   154\u2192\t// A sync.Map is used because in practice sharing of a claim between\n   155\u2192\t// pods is expected to be rare compared to per-pod claim, so we end up\n   156\u2192\t// hitting the \"multiple goroutines read, write, and overwrite entries\n   157\u2192\t// for disjoint sets of keys\" case that sync.Map is optimized for.\n   158\u2192\tinFlightAllocations *sync.Map\n   159\u2192\tallocatedDevices    *allocatedDevices\n   160\u2192\tlogger              klog.Logger\n   161\u2192}\n   162\u2192\n KEY DATA FLOW & INTERACTIONS\n\n#### Prepare Flow:\n1. `kubelet.go:PrepareDynamicResources()` \u2192 \n2. `container_manager_linux.go:PrepareDynamicResources()` \u2192 \n3. `manager.go:PrepareResources()` \u2192\n4. Fetch ResourceClaim from API server \u2192\n5. Group claims by driver/plugin \u2192\n6. Call `dra_plugin.go:NodePrepareResources()` (gRPC to driver) \u2192\n7. Update claim cache with CDI devices \u2192\n8. Checkpoint state to disk\n\n#### Unprepare Flow:\n1. `kubelet.go:UnprepareDynamicResources()` (line 2224) during pod cleanup \u2192\n2. `container_manager_linux.go:UnprepareDynamicResources()` \u2192\n3. `manager.go:UnprepareResources()` \u2192\n4. Call `dra_plugin.go:NodeUnprepareResources()` (gRPC to driver) \u2192\n5. Delete claim from cache \u2192\n6. Checkpoint state to disk\n\n#### Health Monitoring Flow:\n1. `dra_plugin.go:NodeWatchResources()` establishes stream \u2192\n2. `manager.go:HandleWatchResourcesStream()` receives updates \u2192\n3. Updates `healthInfoCache` \u2192\n4. Identifies affected pods and sends update notification \u2192\n5. `UpdateAllocatedResourcesStatus()` updates pod health in status\n\n#### Resource Retrieval for Container:\n1. `container_manager_linux.go:GetResources()` \u2192\n2. `manager.go:GetResources()` \u2192\n3. Query claim cache for CDI devices \u2192\n4. Return `ContainerInfo` with CDI devices \u2192\n5. Used by runtime to inject devices into container\n\n---\n\n### 7. These are errors\n    82\u2192\t// caused by invalid input data, like for example errors in CEL selectors, so a\n    83\u2192\t// scheduler should abort and report that problem instead of trying to find\n    84\u2192\t// other nodes where the error doesn't occur.\n    85\u2192\t//\n    86\u2192\t// In the future, special errors will be defined which enable the caller to\n    87\u2192\t// identify which object (like claim or class) caused the problem. This includes the\n    91\u2192\t// situation where the resource slices are incomplete at the moment.\n    92\u2192\t//\n    93\u2192\t// If the claims can be allocated, then it prepares one allocation result for\n    94\u2192\t// each unallocated claim. It is the responsibility of the caller to persist\n    95\u2192\t// those allocations, if desired.\n    96\u2192\t//\n    97\u2192\t// Allocate is thread-safe. A name can also be useful because log messages do not\n   100\u2192\t// have a common prefix. V(5) is used for one-time log entries, V(6) for important\n   101\u2192\t// progress reports, and V(7) for detailed debug output.\n   102\u2192\t//\n   103\u2192\t//\n   104\u2192\t// Context cancellation is supported. An error wrapping the context's error will\n   105\u2192\t// be returned in case of cancellation.\n   106\u2192\tAllocate(ctx context.Context, node *v1.Node, claims []*resourceapi.ResourceClaim) (finalResult []resourceapi.AllocationResult, finalErr error)\n   107\u2192}\n   108\u2192\n   109\u2192// NewAllocator returns an allocator for a certain set of claims or an error if\n   110\u2192// some problem was detected which makes it impossible to allocate claims.\n   111\u2192//\n   112\u2192// The returned Allocator can be used multiple times and is thread-safe.\n   113\u2192func NewAllocator(ctx context.Context,\n   114\u2192\tfeatures Features,\n   115\u2192\tallocatedState AllocatedState,\n   116\u2192\tclassLister DeviceClassLister,\n   117\u2192\tslices []*resourceapi.ResourceSlice,\n   118\u2192\tcelCache *cel.Cache,\n   119\u2192) (Allocator, error) {\n   120\u2192\t// The actual implementation may vary depending on which features are enabled.\n   121\u2192\t// At the moment there is only one. The goal is to have three:\n   122\u2192\t// - stable: the oldest, most stable code\n   123\u2192\t// - incubating: code which is aiming to become stable next\n   124\u2192\t// - experimental: brand-new code\n   125\u2192\t//\n   126\u2192\t// This corresponds roughly to GA/beta/alpha, but is intentionally not called\n   127\u2192\t// that because e.g. not all features supported by \"stable\" are required to be GA.\n   128\u2192\t//\n   129\u2192\t// Each implementation is completely separate in its own package.\n   130\u2192\t// Common functions are not shared and instead get duplicated to\n   131\u2192\t// keep all implementations completely independent. When comparing\n   132\u2192\t// files, stable should be a subset of incubating and incubating a\n   133\u2192\t// subset of experimental.\n   134\u2192\t//\n   135\u2192\t// Files have a _stable/incubating/experimental suffix to make it obvious\n   136\u2192\t// where log messages come from, although this breaks \"diff -r\".\n   137\u2192\t//\n   138\u2192\t// When \"incubating\" is known to be sufficiently stable, its files can\n   139\u2192\t// be copied wholesale (no editing needed except for the package and\n   140\u2192\t// file name!) into \"stable\", or individual chunks can be copied over.\n   141\u2192\t//\n   142\u2192\t// Unit tests are shared between all implementations.\n   143\u2192\tvar enabledAllocators []string\n   144\u2192\tfor _, allocator := range availableAllocators {\n   145\u2192\t\t// Disabled?\n   146\u2192\t\tif !allocatorEnabled(allocator.name) {\n   147\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   148\u2192\t\t}\n   149\u2192\t\tenabledAllocators = fmt.Errorf(\"internal error: no allocator available for feature set %+v, enabled allocators: %s\", features, strings.Join(enabledAllocators, \", \"))\n   158\u2192}\n   159\u2192\n   160\u2192// \"incubating\", \"experimental\").\n   162\u2192// Not thread-safe, meant for use during testing.\n   163\u2192func EnableAllocators(names ...string) {\n   164\u2192\texplicitlyEnabledAllocators = sets.New(names...)\n   165\u2192}\n   166\u2192\n   167\u2192// explicitlyEnabledAllocators stores the result of EnableAllocators.\n   168\u2192// If empty (the default), all available allocators are *claimName, resourceClaim.UID)\n   301\u2192\t\t}\n   302\u2192\n   303\u2192\t\t// At this point we assume that we have to prepare the claim and thus need\n   304\u2192\t\t// the driver. If the driver is currently unavailable, it is better to fail\n   305\u2192\t\t// even if the claim is already prepared because something is wrong with\n   306\u2192\t\t// the node.\n   307\u2192\t\tinfos[i].resourceClaim = resourceClaim\n   308\u2192\t\tclaimInfo, err := newClaimInfoFromClaim(resourceClaim)\n   309\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   310\u2192\t\t\treturn make(map[string]*draplugin.DRAPlugin, len(claimInfo.DriverState))\n   314\u2192\t\tfor driverName := range claimInfo.DriverState {\n   315\u2192\t\t\tif plugin := infos[i].plugins[driverName]; plugin != nil {\n   316\u2192\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   317\u2192\t\t\t}\n   318\u2192\t\t\tplugin, err := m.draPlugins.GetPlugin(driverName)\n   319\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   320\u2192\t\t\t\t// No wrapping, error includes driver name already.\n   321\u2192\t\t\t\treturn err\n   322\u2192\t\t\t}\n   323\u2192\t\t\tinfos[i].plugins[driverName] = plugin\n   324\u2192\t\t}\n   325\u2192\t}\n   326\u2192\n   327\u2192\t// Now that we have everything that we need, we can update the claim info cache.\n   328\u2192\t// Almost nothing can go wrong anymore at this point.\n   329\u2192\terr = m.cache.withLock(func() error {\n   330\u2192\t\tfor i := range podResourceClaims {\n   331\u2192\t\t\tresourceClaim := infos[i].resourceClaim\n   332\u2192\t\t\tpodClaim := infos[i].podClaim\n   333\u2192\t\t\tif resourceClaim == nil {\n   334\u2192\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"No need to prepare resources, no claim generated\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podClaim\", podClaim.Name)\n 342\u2192\t\t\t\tm.cache.add(claimInfo)\n   343\u2192\t\t\t\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"Created new claim info cache entry\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podClaim\", podClaim.Name, \"claim\", klog.KObj(resourceClaim), \"claimInfoEntry\", claimInfo)\n   344\u2192\t\t\t} else {\n   345\u2192\t\t\t\tif claimInfo.ClaimUID != resourceClaim.UID {\n   346\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"old 348\u2192\t\t\t\tlogger.V(6).Info(\"Found existing claim info cache entry\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podClaim\", podClaim.Name, \"claim\", klog.KObj(resourceClaim), \"claimInfoEntry\", claimInfo)\n   349\u2192\t\t\t}\n   350\u2192\n   351\u2192\t\t\t// Add a reference to the current pod in the claim info.\n   352\u2192\t\t\tclaimInfo.addPodReference(pod.UID)\n   353\u2192\n   354\u2192\t\t\t// prepare call, we will catch\n   357\u2192\t\t\t// that in the reconcile loop and take the appropriate action.\n   358\u2192\t\t\tif err := m.cache.syncToCheckpoint(); err != nil {\n   359\u2192\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"checkpoint ResourceClaim cache: %w\", err)\n   360\u2192\t\t\t}\n   361\u2192\n   362\u2192\t\t\t// If this claim is already prepared, there is no need to prepare it again.\n   363\u2192\t\t\tif claimInfo.isPrepared() {\n   364\u2192\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Resources already prepared\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"podClaim\", podClaim.Name, \"claim\", klog.KObj(resourceClaim))\n   365\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil\n   366\u2192\t\t\t}\n   367\u2192\n   368\u2192\t\t\t// This saved claim will be used to update ClaimInfo cache\n   369\u2192\t\t\t// after NodePrepareResources.\n   373\u2192\t\t\tclaim := &drapb.Claim{\n   374\u2192\t\t\t\tNamespace: claimInfo.Namespace,\n   375\u2192\t\t\t\tUid:       string(claimInfo.ClaimUID),\n   376\u2192\t\t\t\tName:      claimInfo.ClaimName,\n   377\u2192\t\t\t}\n   378\u2192\t\t\tfor driverName := range claimInfo.DriverState {\n   379\u2192\t\t\t\tplugin := infos[i].plugins[driverName]\n   380\u2192\t\t\t\tbatches[plugin] = append(batches[plugin], claim)\n   381\u2192\t\t\t}\n   382\u2192\t\t}\n   383\u2192\n   384\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   385\u2192\t})\n   386\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   387\u2192\t\t// No error wrapping because there is no additional context needed.\n   388\u2192\t\t// What we get here are the errors from our own callback above.\n   389\u2192\t\treturn err\n   390\u2192\t}\n   391\u2192\n   392\u2192\t// Call NodePrepareResources for all claims in each batch.\n   393\u2192\t// If there is any error, processing gets aborted.\n   394\u2192\t// We could try to continue, but that would make the code more complex.\n   395\u2192\tfor plugin, claims := range batches {\n   396\u2192\t\t// Call NodePrepareResources RPC for all resource handles.\n   397\u2192\t\tresponse, err := plugin.NodePrepareResources(ctx, &drapb.NodePrepareResourcesRequest{Claims: claims})\n   398\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   399\u2192\t\t\t// General error unrelated to any 403\u2192\t\t\treqClaim := lookupClaimRequest(claims, claimUID)\n   404\u2192\t\t\tif reqClaim == nil {\n   405\u2192\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"NodePrepareResources returned result for unknown claim 417\u2192\t\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"internal error: unable to get claim info for ResourceClaim %s\", claim.Name)\n   418\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   419\u2192\t\t\t\tfor _, device := range device.CdiDeviceIds})\n   421\u2192\t\t\t\t}\n   422\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil\n   423\u2192\t\t\t})\n   424\u2192\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   425\u2192\t\t\t\t// No wrapping, this is the error above.\n   426\u2192\t\t\t\treturn err\n   427\u2192\t\t\t}\n   428\u2192\t\t}\n   429\u2192\n   430\u2192\t\tunfinished := len(claims) - len(response.Claims)\n   431\u2192\t\tif unfinished != 0 {\n   432\u2192\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"NodePrepareResources skipped %d ResourceClaims\", unfinished)\n   433\u2192\t\t}\n   434\u2192\t}\n   435\u2192\n   436\u2192\t// Atomically perform some operations on the claimInfo cache.\n   437\u2192\terr = m.cache.withLock(func() error {\n   438\u2192\t\t// Mark all pod claims as prepared.\n   439\u2192\t\tfor _, claim := range resourceClaims {\n   440\u2192\t\t\tinfo, exists := m.cache.get(claim.Name, claim.Namespace)\n   441\u2192\t\t\tif !exists {\n   442\u2192\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"internal error: unable to get claim info for with their list\n   448\u2192\t\t// of CDI devices attached.\n   449\u2192\t\tif err := m.cache.syncToCheckpoint(); err != nil {\n   450\u2192\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"checkpoint ResourceClaim state: 457\u2192\t\treturn err\n   458\u2192\t}\n   459\u2192\n   460\u2192\treturn nil\n   461\u2192}\n   462\u2192\n   463\u2192func lookupClaimRequest(claims []*drapb.Claim, claimUID string) *drapb.Claim {\n   464\u2192\tfor _, claim := range claims {\n   465\u2192\t\tif claim.Uid == claimUID {\n   466\u2192\t\t\treturn claim\n   467\u2192\t\t}\n   468\u2192\t}\n   469\u2192\treturn nil\n   470\u2192}\n   471\u2192\n   472\u2192// GetResources gets a ContainerInfo object from the claimInfo cache.\n   473\u2192// This information is used by the caller to update a container config.\n   474\u2192func (m *Manager) GetResources(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) (*ContainerInfo, error) {\n   475\u2192\tcdiDevices := []kubecontainer.CDIDevice{}\n   476\u2192\n   477\u2192\tfor i := 481\u2192\t\t\t// No wrapping, error is already informative.\n   482\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   483\u2192\t\t}\n   484\u2192\t\t// The claim name might be nil if no underlying resource claim\n   485\u2192\t\t// was generated for the referenced claim. anymore.\n   502\u2192\t\t\t\tcdiDevices = append(cdiDevices, claimInfo.cdiDevicesAsList(claim.Request)...)\n   503\u2192\n   504\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil\n   505\u2192\t\t\t})\n   506\u2192\t\t\tif 538\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\t// As of Kubernetes 1.31, CDI device IDs are not passed via annotations anymore.\n   539\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\tcdiDevices = append(cdiDevices, 546\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   547\u2192\t\t}\n   548\u2192\t}\n   549\u2192\treturn &ContainerInfo{CDIDevices: cdiDevices}, nil\n   550\u2192}\n   551\u2192\n   552\u2192// UnprepareResources calls a driver's NodeUnprepareResource API for each resource claim owned by a pod.\n   553\u2192// This function is idempotent and may be called multiple times against the same pod.\n   554\u2192// As such, calls to the underlying NodeUnprepareResource API are skipped for claims that have\n   555\u2192// already been successfully unprepared.\n   556\u2192func (m *Manager) UnprepareResources(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) error {\n   557\u2192\tstartTime := time.Now()\n   558\u2192\terr := m.unprepareResourcesForPod(ctx, pod)\n   559\u2192\tkubeletmetrics.DRAOperationsDuration.WithLabelValues(\"UnprepareResources\", strconv.FormatBool(err == nil)).Observe(time.Since(startTime).Seconds())\n   560\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   561\u2192\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unprepare dynamic resources: %w\", err)\n   562\u2192\t}\n   563\u2192\treturn nil\n   564\u2192}\n   565\u2192\n   566\u2192func (m *Manager) unprepareResourcesForPod(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) error {\n   567\u2192\tvar claimNames []string\n   568\u2192\tfor i := range pod.Spec.ResourceClaims {\n   569\u2192\t\tclaimName, _, err := resourceclaim.Name(pod, &pod.Spec.ResourceClaims[i])\n   570\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   571\u2192\t\t\t// No wrapping, the error is already informative.\n   572\u2192\t\t\treturn err\n   573\u2192\t\t}\n   574\u2192\t\t// The claim name might be nil if no underlying resource claim\n   575\u2192\t\t// was generated for the referenced claim. There are valid use\n   576\u2192\t\t// cases when this might happen, so we simply skip it.\n   577\u2192\t\tif claimName == nil {\n   578\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   579\u2192\t\t}\n   580\u2192\t\tclaimNames = append(claimNames, *claimName)\n   581\u2192\t}\n   582\u2192\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(kubefeatures.DRAExtendedResource) {\n   583\u2192\t\tif pod.Status.ExtendedResourceClaimStatus != nil {\n   584\u2192\t\t\tclaimNames = append(claimNames, pod.Status.ExtendedResourceClaimStatus.ResourceClaimName)\n   585\u2192\t\t}\n   586\u2192\t}\n   587\u2192\n   588\u2192\treturn m.unprepareResources(ctx, pod.UID, pod.Namespace, claimNames)\n   589\u2192}\n   590\u2192\n   591\u2192func (m *Manager) unprepareResources(ctx context.Context, podUID types.UID, namespace string, claimNames []string) error {\n   592\u2192\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   593\u2192\tbatches := make(map[string][]*drapb.Claim)\n   594\u2192\tclaimNamesMap := make(map[types.UID]string)\n   595\u2192\tfor _, claimName := range claimNames {\n   596\u2192\t\t// Atomically perform some operations on the claimInfo cache.\n   597\u2192\t\terr := m.cache.withLock(func() error {\n   598\u2192\t\t\t// Get the claim info from the cache\n   599\u2192\t\t\tclaimInfo, exists := m.cache.get(claimName, namespace)\n   600\u2192\n   601\u2192\t\t\t// Skip calling NodeUnprepareResource if claim info is not cached\n   602\u2192\t\t\tif !exists {\n   603\u2192\t\t\t\treturn nil\n   604\u2192\t\t\t}\n   605\u2192\n   606\u2192\t\t\t// Skip calling NodeUnprepareResource if other pods are still referencing it\n   607\u2192\t\t\tif len(claimInfo.PodUIDs) > 1 {\n   608\u2192\t\t\t\t// We delay checkpointing of this change until\n   609\u2192\t\t\t\t// UnprepareResources returns successfully. It is OK to do\n   610\u2192\t\t\t\t// this because we will only return successfully from this call\n   611\u2192\t\t\t\t// if the checkpoint has succeeded. 635\u2192\t\t\t// No wrapping, this is the error above.\n   636\u2192\t\t\treturn err\n   637\u2192\t\t}\n   638\u2192\t}\n   639\u2192\n   640\u2192\t// Call NodeUnprepareResources for all claims in each batch.\n   641\u2192\t// If there is any error, processing gets aborted.\n   642\u2192\t// We could try to continue, but that would make the code more complex.\n   643\u2192\tfor driverName, claims := range batches {\n   644\u2192\t\t// Call NodeUnprepareResources RPC for all resource handles.\n   645\u2192\t\tplugin, err := m.draPlugins.GetPlugin(driverName)\n   646\u2192\t\tif plugin == nil {\n   647\u2192\t\t\t// No wrapping, error includes driver name already.\n   648\u2192\t\t\treturn err\n   649\u2192\t\t}\n   650\u2192\t\tresponse, err := plugin.NodeUnprepareResources(ctx, &drapb.NodeUnprepareResourcesRequest{Claims: claims})\n   651\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   652\u2192\t\t\t// General error unrelated to any particular claim.\n   653\u2192\t\t\treturn     "content": "/*\nCopyright 2024 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\npackage stable\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"fmt\"\n\n\tv1 \"k8s.io/api/core/v1\"\n\tresourceapi \"k8s.io/api/resource/v1\"\n\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets\"\n\t\"k8s.io/component-helpers/scheduling/corev1/nodeaffinity\"\n\tdraapi \"k8s.io/dynamic-resource-allocation/api\"\n\t\"k8s.io/utils/ptr\"\n)\n\nfunc nodeMatches(node *v1.Node, nodeNameToMatch string, allNodesMatch bool, nodeSelector *v1.NodeSelector) (bool, error) {\n\tswitch {\n\tcase nodeNameToMatch != \"\":\n\t\treturn node != nil && node.Name == nodeNameToMatch, nil\n\tcase allNodesMatch:\n\t\treturn true, nil\n\tcase nodeSelector != nil:\n\t\tselector, err := nodeaffinity.NewNodeSelector(nodeSelector)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn false, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to parse node selector %s: %w\", nodeSelector.String(), err)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn selector.Match(node), nil\n\t}\n\n\treturn false, nil\n}\n\ntype poolIdentifier struct {\n\tdriver, pool string\n}\n\n// GatherPools collects information about all resource pools which provide\n// devices that are accessible from the given node.\n//\n// Out-dated slices are silently ignored. Pools may be incomplete (not all\n// required slices available) or invalid (for example, device names not unique).\n// Both is recorded in the result.\nfunc GatherPools(ctx context.Context, slices []*resourceapi.ResourceSlice, node *v1.Node, features Features) ([]*Pool, error) {\n\tslicesByPool := make(map[poolIdentifier][]*resourceapi.ResourceSlice)\n\tfor _, slice := range slices {\n\t\tpoolID := poolIdentifier{\n\t\t\tdriver: slice.Spec.Driver,\n\t\t\tpool:   slice.Spec.Pool.Name,\n\t\t}\n\t\tslicesByPool[poolID] = append(slicesByPool[poolID], slice)\n\t}\n\n\t// We need to check whether a pool is complete while we have all\n\t// the slices. Once we discard slices that don't target the node, we\n\t// no longer have the information needed to find out.\n\tincompletePools := sets.New[poolIdentifier]()\n\tfor poolID, slices := range slicesByPool {\n\t\tcomplete := true\n\t\tsliceCount := len(slices)\n\t\tgeneration := slices[0].Spec.Pool.Generation\n\t\tfor _, slice := range slices {\n\t\t\t// If the number of slices in the pool specified in any of the slices\n\t\t\t// doesn't match what we found, the pool is most likely being updated\n\t\t\t// by the controller.\n\t\t\tif slice.Spec.Pool.ResourceSliceCount != int64(sliceCount) {\n\t\t\t\tcomplete = false\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// If the generation of the pool isn't the same across all slices,\n\t\t\t// the pool is most likely being updated by the controller. We can't\n\t\t\t// allocate devices from it.\n\t\t\tif slice.Spec.Pool.Generation != generation {\n\t\t\t\tcomplete = false\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\t// We still need to keep incomplete pools, since we need to make sure\n\t\t// all devices available on a node is considered for allocationMode All.\n\t\tif !complete {\n\t\t\tincompletePools.Insert(poolID)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tpools := make(map[PoolID]*Pool)\n\tfor _, slice := range slices {\n\t\tif !features.PartitionableDevices && slice.Spec.PerDeviceNodeSelection != nil {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif nodeName, allNodes := ptr.Deref(slice.Spec.NodeName, \"\"), ptr.Deref(slice.Spec.AllNodes, false); nodeName != \"\" || allNodes || slice.Spec.NodeSelector != nil {\n\t\t\tmatch, err := nodeMatches(node, nodeName, allNodes, slice.Spec.NodeSelector)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to perform node selection for slice %s: %w\", slice.Name, err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif match {\n\t\t\t\tif err := addSlice(pools, slice); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to add node slice %s: %w\", slice.Name, err)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else if ptr.Deref(slice.Spec.PerDeviceNodeSelection, false) {\n\t\t\tfor _, device := range slice.Spec.Devices {\n\t\t\t\tmatch, err := nodeMatches(node, ptr.Deref(device.NodeName, \"\"), ptr.Deref(device.AllNodes, false), device.NodeSelector)\n\t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to perform node selection for device %s in slice %s: %w\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\tdevice.String(), slice.Name, err)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tif match {\n\t\t\t\t\tif err := addSlice(pools, slice); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to add node slice %s: %w\", slice.Name, err)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// Nothing known was set. This must be some future, unknown extension,\n\t\t\t// so we don't know how to handle it. We may still be able to allocated from\n\t\t\t// other pools, so we continue.\n\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t// TODO (eventually): let caller decide how to report this to the user. Warning\n\t\t\t// about it for every slice on each scheduling attempt would be too noisy, but\n\t\t\t// perhaps once per run would be useful?\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t}\n\n\t// Find incomplete pools and flatten into a single slice.\n\tresult := make([]*Pool, 0, len(pools))\n\tfor _, pool := range pools {\n\t\tpool.IsIncomplete = incompletePools.Has(poolIdentifier{driver: pool.Driver.String(), pool: pool.Pool.String()})\n\t\tpool.IsInvalid, pool.InvalidReason = poolIsInvalid(pool)\n\t\tresult = append(result, pool)\n\t}\n\n\treturn result, nil\n}\n\nfunc addSlice(pools map[PoolID]*Pool, s *resourceapi.ResourceSlice) error {\n\tvar slice draapi.ResourceSlice\n\tif err := draapi.Convert_v1_ResourceSlice_To_api_ResourceSlice(s, &slice, nil); err != nil {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"convert ResourceSlice: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tid := PoolID{Driver: slice.Spec.Driver, Pool: slice.Spec.Pool.Name}\n\tpool := pools[id]\n\tif pool == nil {\n\t\t// New pool.\n\t\tpool = &Pool{\n\t\t\tPoolID: id,\n\t\t\tSlices: []*draapi.ResourceSlice{&slice},\n\t\t}\n\t\tpools[id] = pool\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tif slice.Spec.Pool.Generation < pool.Slices[0].Spec.Pool.Generation {\n\t\t// Out-dated.\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tif slice.Spec.Pool.Generation > pool.Slices[0].Spec.Pool.Generation {\n\t\t// Newer, replaces all old slices.\n\t\tpool.Slices = nil\n\t}\n\n\t// Add to pool.\n\tpool.Slices = append(pool.Slices, &slice)\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc poolIsInvalid(pool *Pool) (bool, string) {\n\tdevices := sets.New[draapi.UniqueString]()\n\tfor _, slice := range pool.Slices {\n\t\tfor _, device := range slice.Spec.Devices {\n\t\t\tif devices.Has(device.Name) {\n\t\t\t\treturn true, fmt.Sprintf(\"duplicate device name %s\", device.Name)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tdevices.Insert(device.Name)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn false, \"\"\n}\n\ntype Pool struct {\n\tPoolID\n\tIsIncomplete  bool\n\tIsInvalid     bool\n\tInvalidReason string\n\tSlices        []*draapi.ResourceSlice\n}\n\ntype PoolID struct {\n\tDriver, Pool draapi.UniqueString\n}\n\nfunc (p PoolID) String() string {\n\treturn p.Driver.String() + \"/\" + p.Pool.String()\n}\n",
